class=\"icon log\"></span><span class=\"count\"></span><pre class=\"text\"></pre></div>"],"text":["S1 failing two exams in(b) makes us think that the posterior of exam being hard and the student didn't study should increase than priors and our intuition matches graphs in b. When we see two more students failed in the same exams, we start thinking that the posterior of exam of being hard and S1 studied conditioned on all these should increase even more than those of (b)because perhaps S1 studied but failed for difficulty in E1 like other students and our intuition matches the graphs in(c)too. ","Along with conditions in(b)and (c), when we see S2,S3 has failed other exams too, we think perhaps s2 and s3 didn't study and hence failed all the exams, so the posterior of e1 is easy should should be higher than (c).We don't expect s2,s3's fail in E3,E4 to impact s1's study habit because s1's earlier study habit was determined byperformance in E1 and E2 and we know nothing about his performance in E3,E4. So other people's performance there won't affect his study habit and graph in d show that.","When we see S1 passing E3,E4, we feel that posterior of S1 studied should increase. We also feel that since he passed other two exams, the reason he failed E1 might be its difficulty. So intuitively we expect the posterior of E1 being hard and S1 studied to increase. We see those changes in (e). Apparently, the posterior that S1 studied increased a lot.The posterior that E1 was hard didn't increase too much but still increased.","Collecting data from 3 people and averaging that, people's estimate that S1 studied and E1 easy given conditions in (b),(c),(d),(e) are respectively 0.2,0.46,0.46,0.766 and 0.733,0.3,0.333,0.1.Posteriors from model are 0.09,0.1,0.1,0.37 and 0.67,0.31,0.34,0.31. Apparently, the shift is in the right direction. Correlation(human judgement, correct probability)=0.866 for s1's study habit and correlation(human judgement,correct prob)=0.94 for exam's easiness.Everyone including me overestimated s1's probability of studying in each case but the posteriors of exam's difficulty is almost similar to human judgment and this is reflected in the coefficient.In real life we see that most people study or try hard even if they are failing. This can be a reason why we are overestimating these posteriors.","Qauntitaive shift in the bayes net.Earlier in (b)-(d), the posterior of S1 studied was around 0.1 and here it is around 0.2 and didn't deviate that much from that which we see in the earlier case too.Then the posterior in (e) became almost 3 times of (d)(0.37) in earlier case and the same happened in later case too(from .2 to .58).The posteriors of E1 easy was around 0.32 in (c)-(e) in earlier case and in latter case it was around (0.2), and the deviation from these values in both cases was really small.(b) in earlier case has a posterior of 0.67 and 0.52 in latter case. The shifts are also in the direction of our intuition.We increased study prior and decreased exam's easiness prior and the overall shifts maintains that too.","We see posterior of prof's leniency and an exam being advanced decreasing in part (b)-(d).In (e) this trend is reversed. Whether or not a student passes an exam depends on if that student studied and if exam was easy. If the professor is lenient, exams will be easy with high probability, so most students will pass. If a class is advanced,students will study with higher probability, so most students will pass too.(b)-(d) all shows more and more incidents of failure in exams, so we see how posterior of prof's lenience and exam's advancedness keeps dropping.(e) is the first time we introduce an incident of passing which works in favor of exam's easiness and student is studying and these two respectively works in favor of posterior of professor's lenience and course's advancedness","My intuition matches the model predictions.When S1 fails an exam, we tend to think that he is more likely to be sleepy than to be not sleepy because the overall pass probabilties in all cases while non sleepy is higher. But when we get 3 more students failed the same exam, we think that it is perhaps not that S1 was sleepy, it was perhaps that exam was difficult.We see this reflection in the graph too. The posterior of s1 being sleepy during E1 in first case raised from 0.5 to 0.66. Then we find 3 more students failing the same exam which increases the posterior of exam being hard which in turn decreases the posterior of S1 being sleepy.",""],"savedAt":"10/11/2020 1:34:44 AM"}
